<div id="review_766475326" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/766475326" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/766475326?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=this-book-is-everything">this-book-is-everything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=gurrrl-power">gurrrl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=hot-guys-alphas-rawr">hot-guys-alphas-rawr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-vampires">fantasy-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-urban">fantasy-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-witches-and-wizards">fantasy-witches-and-wizards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-werewolves-and-shifters">fantasy-werewolves-and-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer766475326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12816246870486870841">When I started these books, I liked them, but I didn't love them. Then, I think it was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30260.A_Fistful_of_Charms__The_Hollows___4_' title='A Fistful of Charms (The Hollows, #4) by Kim Harrison' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Fistful of Charms</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30259.For_a_Few_Demons_More__The_Hollows___5_' title='For a Few Demons More (The Hollows, #5) by Kim Harrison' rel='nofollow noopener'>For a Few Demons More</a> that I really started to enjoy the series and felt fully committed. Then, for a couple books, I felt they were okay, but just okay. Not a fan of the banshee book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3475268.White_Witch__Black_Curse__The_Hollows___7_' title='White Witch, Black Curse (The Hollows, #7) by Kim Harrison' rel='nofollow noopener'>White Witch, Black Curse</a>, but then I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6547188.Black_Magic_Sanction__The_Hollows___8_' title='Black Magic Sanction (The Hollows, #8) by Kim Harrison' rel='nofollow noopener'>Black Magic Sanction</a> and I LOVED it, LOVED it! But THEN, I just finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8138071.Pale_Demon__The_Hollows___9_' title='Pale Demon (The Hollows, #9) by Kim Harrison' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pale Demon</a> and Kim Harrison has now been solidified as genius in my book. <br/><br/>This may be one</span>
  <span id="freeText12816246870486870841" style="display:none">When I started these books, I liked them, but I didn't love them. Then, I think it was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30260.A_Fistful_of_Charms__The_Hollows___4_" title="A Fistful of Charms (The Hollows, #4) by Kim Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">A Fistful of Charms</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30259.For_a_Few_Demons_More__The_Hollows___5_" title="For a Few Demons More (The Hollows, #5) by Kim Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">For a Few Demons More</a> that I really started to enjoy the series and felt fully committed. Then, for a couple books, I felt they were okay, but just okay. Not a fan of the banshee book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3475268.White_Witch__Black_Curse__The_Hollows___7_" title="White Witch, Black Curse (The Hollows, #7) by Kim Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">White Witch, Black Curse</a>, but then I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6547188.Black_Magic_Sanction__The_Hollows___8_" title="Black Magic Sanction (The Hollows, #8) by Kim Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Magic Sanction</a> and I LOVED it, LOVED it! But THEN, I just finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8138071.Pale_Demon__The_Hollows___9_" title="Pale Demon (The Hollows, #9) by Kim Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Pale Demon</a> and Kim Harrison has now been solidified as genius in my book. <br /><br />This may be one of the best books I have ever read, at the very least, in this genre. I really think this author is brilliant. Who knew, by book NINE in a series, that it would be (arguably) the best in the whole freaking thing (to this point)! <br /><br />The way the whole story unfolded, and I won't even get into the details, but this is among the finest story-telling I've ever read. I love Al. I never was a Pierce fan, but dang, if he doesn't prove himself to be amazing in this. Trent is all over this one, and you will be shocked to see what unfolds with him. So much good stuff.<br /><br />SPOILERISH The ending, understandably, is, well, I can't blame Rachel for trying, but we all know, her reprieve will be brief. She will not be able to keep that charmed bracelet on. She will have to get her REAL magic back. My big thing was, how can she keep her surviving it all from Al? He is going to be so hurt that she didn't tell him and chose to hide herself from him. I feel bad for him. She should have went to him. I think you start to feel a lot more sympathy for the demons after this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12816246870486870841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13375041450598361158">Whew! I'm so excited about this book, there are no words to express it! It is my new favorite in the series!!!!! I did struggle just a bit with the last book, and this one took all the loose ends and made sense of everything!<br/><br/>It was action packed, so much happened, so much changed, and then changed again, and again! We got to see a new side to some of our favorite characters, were able to really understand others.<br/><br/>It also has plenty of romance, considering Rachel's love life is such a complicated </span>
  <span id="freeText13375041450598361158" style="display:none">Whew! I'm so excited about this book, there are no words to express it! It is my new favorite in the series!!!!! I did struggle just a bit with the last book, and this one took all the loose ends and made sense of everything!<br /><br />It was action packed, so much happened, so much changed, and then changed again, and again! We got to see a new side to some of our favorite characters, were able to really understand others.<br /><br />It also has plenty of romance, considering Rachel's love life is such a complicated mess. As a Trent/Rachel fan from book 1, I'll admit this book has something in store for you no what who you want Rachel to end up with: Al, Trent, Pierce or Ivy.<br /><br />Rachel is really growing into her powers, and as things changed many times as far as where the story can go from here, at the end, I hope she chooses to continue on and explore her powers!!!!<br /><br />The actual trip across to the West Coast was a riot! However, I did hit a slump in the reading excitement once we were stuck in the Ever After. Don't really know why, because everything that happened there was interesting, I may have to go back and re-read that part again! Maybe among other parts I'd like to re-read ;) hehe <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The kiss!!!!!! I almost fainted when Rachel got into it and pushed him against the refrigerator!!!! Of course, Trent naked coming out of the shower! And then when he was getting dressed to go on his elf quest, with Rachel lusting after him, and he notices her looking and teases her!!! OMG <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I don't want to give too much away from the story, so I'll address the characters individually.<br /><br />Rachel: I was happy to find her back to her usual self, without the constant complaining about whether she's a white witch, or a black witch, and she took care of her own destiny! She was confident, she stood her ground with all the characters and situations.<br /><br />Trent: We get to see a completely new side of him, or is it just that there's a playful elf underneath all that serious businessman, drug-lord façade? I've always said that he had some growing up to do, and that he slowly had to come to terms with some things, and he's showing us he can def do it! I'm so excited about next books can bring us. And he gives us a surprise that was completely out of left field for me, it just left me with my mouth hanging open!!! What?!?!? Enough said! It was too sweet!!!!!<br /><br />Jenks: I LOVE Jenks. Every moment, every comment! He's the funniest little pixie around. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I mean, he gets kidnapped because they want to mate with him!?!?!? And I think it's really cute how there's a moment to express his crush for TinkerBell and he actually goes to her exhibit at Disneyland.... LMAO <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He has gone through so much after loosing Madelina and I feel that he's adapting well in this book.<br /><br />Ivy: I was happy to find a little bit of closure to the constant Ivy/Rachel thing, although I've heard it may not be a permanent thing. Don't get me wrong, I think she's cool, and we got to see an emotional side to her, I agree she has to move on!<br /><br />Bis: I wish we would've seen more of him!!!!<br /><br />Pierce: I wanted to kill him most of the book. I don't know why I just don't like him, never have, prob never will.<br /><br />Newt: She's actually really funny!<br /><br />And last but not least, AL!: He is as funny as always, a liked him a little better in this book. I wish we knew what he really looks like! We also see another side of him in this book and I enjoyed that!<br /><br />In conclusion, it was awesome, it reignited the spark of this series for me, and CANNOT wait for the next book. Does it really have to take a whole year?!?!?!?!<br /><br /><b>Ivy's Song: Cake - Short Skirt, Long Jacket</b><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=X5KmB8Laemg" rel="nofollow noopener">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=X5KmB8Laemg</a></span>

<div id="review_129123448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129123448" />
    <a title="Deea (Andreea)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3017446-deea-andreea"><img alt="Deea (Andreea)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290530927p2/3017446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129123448?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deea (Andreea)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deea (Andreea)" href="/user/show/3017446-deea-andreea">Deea (Andreea)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3017446-deea-andreea?shelf=epic-reads">epic-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3017446-deea-andreea?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3017446-deea-andreea?shelf=uf">uf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129123448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7390579131612688518"><b>*Re-read July 2015*</b><br/><br/>Just as spectacular as the first time - and second time, or however many times - I read it! Or maybe even more so, now that I could just sit back and read at a slower pace, enjoying the ride and reading through the lines, looking for the hidden clues and subtle messages. And being closer to the end of the series now, I could see certain things in a different light and what a game changer this book was for the entire story. Like I said in my initial review, I loved how all my f</span>
  <span id="freeText7390579131612688518" style="display:none"><b>*Re-read July 2015*</b><br /><br />Just as spectacular as the first time - and second time, or however many times - I read it! Or maybe even more so, now that I could just sit back and read at a slower pace, enjoying the ride and reading through the lines, looking for the hidden clues and subtle messages. And being closer to the end of the series now, I could see certain things in a different light and what a game changer this book was for the entire story. Like I said in my initial review, I loved how all my favorite characters had a role to play and how much their relationship, dynamics and overall personalities developed. As always, I'm in awe of Kim Harrison's talent and ways of crafting, building and spinning everything, to every little detail and word said. <br /><br />Whatever, I'm fangirling, but I'm happy I can still enjoy this series so much years later! That shit is rare nowadays, my friends! :D<br /><br /> <br /><br />_________________________________________<br /><br />***January 2011***<br /><a href="http://deeas-journal.blogspot.com/2011/02/review-pale-demon-hollows-9-by-kim.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Pale Demon review on my blog</a><br />First off, I need to say that I finally understand why people say this book is THE BOOK of the series and why it is everyone's favorite - it's mine too. It has it all: great humor, non-stop action, nail-bitting suspense, strong, like-able characters, and just a touch of romance, enough to make your heart beat loudly in your chest. I love, love, love it!<br /><br />It could be because all my favorite characters are brought together on a hell of a road-trip and they all showed the best in them. I was smiling throughout the whole book - if I wasn’ t laughing out loud or staring open-mouthed at the page, that is. If in other books of the series sometimes I felt like slapping Rachel because of her decisions, in this one she has me completely on her side. She proves just how strong she is, how much she cares about her friends and she even starts to accept her past actions and who she really is. It's like she finally grows up.<br /><br />Ivy was there in the right place in the right time, as always, but I would have liked to see more of her character. I think Jenks had some better moments in the previous books, but he’ s still the most adorable and fun character and a reliable addition to the team. Oh, and I still don’ t like Pierce – actually, at some point I was wondering why didn’ t someone just kill him right then, right there. And Trent… well…*inserts dreamy sigh here* he is quite a piece of work! I was glad because I could finally get him better, he was a constant (infuriating and delicious) presence in this book. As I was reading, I even wanted to hug him or to slap him silly or just to jump him!:)) I don't want to spoil the book for you, but there are some pretty nice teasing moments that will make any Trent fan swoon.<br /><br />There were also some touchy moments that I really liked, because they gave me the chance to feel more connected to the characters and to understand them better. I missed this kind of scenes in the last couple of books.<br /><br />All in all, it was a very enjoyable read and the ending was very satisfying – it wasn’ t a cliff hanger to make me pull my hair out in frustration until the next book came out, but it was still open, with a lot of unanswered questions and possibilities, so I can't wait to see what happens next!<br />Fun, fast-paced and with a lot of twists and turns to keep you entertained, Pale Demon is indeed the book of the series. Kim Harrison is a fabulous writer and a great storyteller, who made me close the door to reality completely and devour every page of her book - and always eager to read more of her work!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7390579131612688518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_527159842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527159842" />
    <a title="Jane Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart"><img alt="Jane Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527159842?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062087607" href="/book/show/13621486-pale-demon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527159842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2409128545004811272">I was bored. I wanted it to be over.<br/><br/>This is book 9. I feel like the author has nothing left to write about. It’s lots of conversation about very little. When bad guys appear, Rachel solves the problem by pulling on a ley line and using magic.<br/><br/>My biggest problem is I don’t like Rachel. She doesn’t show humility. She acts like a bratty snotty teenager. Most of the time she argues, gets angry, and threatens. There is a lot of “You did this? Well I’m going to do that to you.”<br/><br/>Trent enthrals two assass</span>
  <span id="freeText2409128545004811272" style="display:none">I was bored. I wanted it to be over.<br /><br />This is book 9. I feel like the author has nothing left to write about. It’s lots of conversation about very little. When bad guys appear, Rachel solves the problem by pulling on a ley line and using magic.<br /><br />My biggest problem is I don’t like Rachel. She doesn’t show humility. She acts like a bratty snotty teenager. Most of the time she argues, gets angry, and threatens. There is a lot of “You did this? Well I’m going to do that to you.”<br /><br />Trent enthrals two assassins so he can ask them who sent them. The enthral only lasts a couple of minutes. Rachel is furious and argues with Trent because his enthral used “black magic.” She wasted time instead of asking the assassins who sent them. Finally Jenks and Ivy interrupted Rachel’s rant and asked the assassins who sent them. I was not interested in watching Rachel do this.<br /><br />The author used contrivances to create suspense which annoyed me. For example, someone tells Rachel to plead guilty, go to jail, don’t worry, I have a plan. But he doesn’t tell her the plan. So for a long time Rachel is worried and there is a lot of angst. I would rather just see how the trial and things worked out instead of someone saying “I have a plan, but I’m not going to tell you.”<br /><br />More contrivance examples. Rachel rushes in yelling “they took him...they took him.” After a minute Trent gets out of the shower and says “took who?”<br /><br />Rachel makes statements like “It didn’t work.” A minute later the reader hears that it did work.<br /><br />The word clench was over used. I felt like it was used on every other page. There is teeth clenched, jaw clenched, gut clenched, fingers clenched, hands clenched, my heart seemed to clench, worry clenched my chest, we both clenched in pain, stomach clenched, clenched my eyes, my gut unclenched as it grew quiet.<br /><br />I listened to the first 15 hours and couldn’t take any more. So I jumped to the last chapter and was glad to be out.<br /><br />THE HOLLOWS (RACHEL MORGAN) SERIES:<br />As of 2013 there are 11 books in the series. Sadly it’s not for me, but I gave it a try. The three I read are:<br />3 stars. Dead Witch Walking, Book 1<br />2 stars. The Good, the Bad, and the Undead, Book 2<br />1 star. Pale Demon, Book 9<br /><br />DATA:<br />Narrative mode: 1st person Rachel. Unabridged audiobook length: 17 hrs and 54 mins. Swearing language: strong but rarely used. Sexual content: none in the first 15 hours. Setting: time similar to current day various U.S. locations. Book copyright: 2011. Genre: urban fantasy.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166233737" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=e-pcs">e-pcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=highly-rated">highly-rated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=hyped">hyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-urban-fantasy">genre-urban-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166233737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17740931024667550192"><b>MY FIRST FIVE STAR RATING FOR THE HOLLOWS SERIES...<br/>WHAT AN AWESOME BOOK!!!!!!!!!</b><br/><br/>Now, I've never really disliked any of this series, or I'd never have continued reading. But I've never been truly gaga over it like some either. Until this book. What a multifaceted, much anticipated story that takes place in Pale Demon!!<br/><br/>Rachel is on her way across the country to attend her brother's wedding. But her fellow road trippers not only include Jenks and Ivy (always trouble with those three) but also.....T</span>
  <span id="freeText17740931024667550192" style="display:none"><b>MY FIRST FIVE STAR RATING FOR THE HOLLOWS SERIES...<br />WHAT AN AWESOME BOOK!!!!!!!!!</b><br /><br />Now, I've never really disliked any of this series, or I'd never have continued reading. But I've never been truly gaga over it like some either. Until this book. What a multifaceted, much anticipated story that takes place in Pale Demon!!<br /><br />Rachel is on her way across the country to attend her brother's wedding. But her fellow road trippers not only include Jenks and Ivy (always trouble with those three) but also.....Trenton Kalamack!!!! Oh, yes...Trent and Rachel in a car for hours on end. Too bad they weren't alone.<br /><br />Thing is, Harrison still doesn't ever write an overtly romantic scene. But if you're a fan of the series, or if, like me, it's juuuust interesting enough, you know there's more to him. I could never put my finger on it. He's one of those characters that you can't force into revealing his secrets. But during the last couple of books, I feel like Harrison has really been leading us to this book. Trent and Rachel's antagonistic relationship has always been so volatile. It's no different here, but rest assured that their odd sort of understanding takes huge steps forward during the course of this story. <br /><br />Rachel and Al also have an odd sort of relationship, and though Al has truly pulled off some evil doings, I still kind of like the crazy demon. He obviously has a thing for Rachel. And it's not just attraction. There are feelings involved, so he can't be all bad, right? Ah, whatever...I'm such a romance reader, I see romance everywhere. <br /><br />Suffice it to say that this book is almost nonstop action, nonstop revelations, and...do I FINALLY see an end to the weird, uncomfortable thing going on between Ivy and Rachel? God, I hope so. What an awkward, guilt-riddled friendship. It's always annoyed me.<br /><br />I'm so glad to have read this book. The series needed this. It moved forward by leaps and bounds within the pages of Pale Demon, and renewed my fascination with the Hollows.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17740931024667550192" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16530119469579615244">Easily the best book in the series so far! Rachel has to get to the west coast for the witch counsel to decide her fate. Trent has a mysterious mission he has to head out west for, so road trip time! I’ve gotta admit it got off to a rocky start. Trent was being a complete and utter asshat, and Rachel was whiny and irritating. Then it got wicked good once the demons got involved.<br/><br/>Al was awesome! He was my favorite character in the book. Spending some time with him in the ever after made some of hi</span>
  <span id="freeText16530119469579615244" style="display:none">Easily the best book in the series so far! Rachel has to get to the west coast for the witch counsel to decide her fate. Trent has a mysterious mission he has to head out west for, so road trip time! I’ve gotta admit it got off to a rocky start. Trent was being a complete and utter asshat, and Rachel was whiny and irritating. Then it got wicked good once the demons got involved.<br /><br />Al was awesome! He was my favorite character in the book. Spending some time with him in the ever after made some of his past despicable actions make more sense. I love it that he and Rachel are getting along. Once and for all it’s finally been proven that Rachel is a demon.<br /><br />It was great that Ivy only had a minor role. I never liked Pierce. He really pissed me off with what he tried to do. The results of Trent’s elf quest were surprising. Trent’s arrogance could have gotten them killed. There was a method to his madness. It was not the best plan although the events in St. Louis were entertaining. This book got better and better as it went along. I’m really looking forward to the next one.<br /></span>

<div id="review_144208663" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144208663" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144208663?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144208663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4761781850515191743">Ninth in the paranormal/urban fantasy series, The Hollows, starring Rachel Morgan, <em>Pale Demon</em> follows along with the general theme of titles twisted along Clint Eastwood movies, although it doesn't have the same kick as the earlier books.<br/><br/>In 2011, <em>Pale Demon</em> was nominated for the Goodreads Choice Award for Best Paranormal Fantasy.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>Harrison's got us twisting in the wind with all the coils and snaking loops interspersed throughout <em>Pale Demon</em>. Rachel does make a huge impression on the witches </span>
  <span id="freeText4761781850515191743" style="display:none">Ninth in the paranormal/urban fantasy series, The Hollows, starring Rachel Morgan, <em>Pale Demon</em> follows along with the general theme of titles twisted along Clint Eastwood movies, although it doesn't have the same kick as the earlier books.<br /><br />In 2011, <em>Pale Demon</em> was nominated for the Goodreads Choice Award for Best Paranormal Fantasy.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />Harrison's got us twisting in the wind with all the coils and snaking loops interspersed throughout <em>Pale Demon</em>. Rachel does make a huge impression on the witches and the council, and between her and Pierce, I suspect some changes to be coming. Then there's Trent's little surprise. Just how this is going to change elven futures is something for our own future reading.<br /><br />I so cannot wait until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10599805-a-perfect-blood" title="Opens Kim Harrison's A Perfect Blood in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>A Perfect Blood</em>
</a> to find out what happens next. Ivy's threats, the I.S.'s promise, Rachel's new abilities, Trent's reactions to Rachel and his young creation, the coven's responses…oh man, it is going to be good!<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />This is it. The moment for which Rachel has been waiting. She can finally clear her name and get the shunning rescinded in San Francisco at the witches' convention. There are just a few roadblocks along the way and Trent is pushing her to bodyguard him to the Coast. It's a pain, but road trip seems to be the only way to get past the roadblocks.<br /><br />Unfortunately, now we have "adventures" and, oh man, is Rachel busy along the way. Even more unfortunately, so is Trent…busy that is. Kidnappings, day-walking demons, earthquake, destruction, a coven council spy on her tail…ah well, all in a day's work for Rachel until the conference when Oliver reneges on the deal, and Rachel freefalls into a nightmare.<br /><br />Learning all sorts of new things with very few of them welcome. Those power tests can be a menace, but then the coven needs her back in San Francisco to save their collective butts. Oh yeah, karma can be a bitch.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Rachel Morgan</strong> is a good witch who just happens to work black magic which makes just about everyone in her world (and out of it) after her and not in a good way. <strong>Jenks</strong> is her pixie sidekick still mourning <strong>Matalina</strong>, which turns into a trap. <strong>Ivy tamwood</strong> is a living vampire partnered up and living in a converted church with Rachel. <strong>Pierce</strong> is a come-back-to-life former member of the coven council in love with Rachel…we think…who is thoroughly involved in black magic.<br /><br /><strong>Ku'Sox</strong> is a demon nightmare come back to life. <strong>Al</strong> is a demon with a hold on Rachel. One minute he's taking care of her and the next…eek!! Then there's <strong>Newt</strong> — every demon is afraid of her ‘cause she's not only powerful but nuts.<br /><br /><em>The witches' coven council includes…</em><br />…<strong>Vivian</strong>, <strong>Oliver</strong>, <strong>Leon</strong>, <strong>Wyatt</strong>, and <strong>Amanda</strong> who all have a major desire for Rachel's non-existence, although Vivian seems to be more open-minded since her last clashes with Rachel.<br /><br /><em>Inderland Security is…</em><br />…the supernatural legal authority (consider it a state and federal FBI) in this new version of Earth after the Turn, and they've had it out for Rachel for years and they make a brief and… surprising…appearance.<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />Oh, so, definitely a hot dress! I want one…of course, I'd need the body too. The cover is perfect — Rachel channeling the energies in her form-fitting, laced-up-the-back, short, white leather dress with her red hair in a braid. Go Rache!<br /><br />The title refers to Rachel, for she's the <em>Pale Demon</em> who has everyone terrified.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4761781850515191743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136807286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3730531412776801524">Three and a half stars, rounding up to 4.<br/><br/>I'd been losing interest in the Rachel Morgan series for a while because she was too static a character. Her emotional reactions in book #8 were virtually identical to book#1 (self-doubt, compensating rush to intimacy, fear and pulling-away, self-berating, failed attempt to regain intimacy), and I just think it's time for her to grow up. Frequently had a bipolar reaction during confrontations, and that's still present here: pretending to be disinterested/</span>
  <span id="freeText3730531412776801524" style="display:none">Three and a half stars, rounding up to 4.<br /><br />I'd been losing interest in the Rachel Morgan series for a while because she was too static a character. Her emotional reactions in book #8 were virtually identical to book#1 (self-doubt, compensating rush to intimacy, fear and pulling-away, self-berating, failed attempt to regain intimacy), and I just think it's time for her to grow up. Frequently had a bipolar reaction during confrontations, and that's still present here: pretending to be disinterested/in control, then disdainful, then flirty and escalating to shouting/violence. Same stuff, different books. Maybe because I've let the series slide, or because Rachel <i>is</i> growing up a little bit, I enjoyed this book a bit more. She is still making the mistake of refusing to do something on principle, but then ending up doing that very thing moments later. Thankfully, once she gets in the car with Trent, that moment is over. I'm not sure if that's the only way Harrison knows how to write Rachel's motivation, or if that's all her character's got. As I said, it's one of the main reasons I've lost interest in Rachel, and she no longer comes close to favorite UF heroine. <br /><br />Readers might also have trouble with Trent's mysterious elven quest and it's results. An attempt is made to modernize the quest analogy, but it falls a little flat, since it's so mysterious, no one can know anything about it until it's over. It's a quest of dubious ethical standards, and it's unfortunate that Rachel falls for the result. I don't think Harrison set it up enough that the reader can feel confident Trent and Jenks acted by a moral standard, and Rachel becomes complicit in the results. I also question to what extent his success will allow him to "control the future of the elven race." If he is sincere, Rachel should run, run, run, because he is still viewing other people and entities as means to an end. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The fact that he released an "ultimate evil" kind of demon as a means to manipulate the witches' council into forgiving Rachel is a perfect example of how he has crossed the line into scary.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I've always kind of liked Trent and thought Rachel/ Harrison has a soft spot for him as well; we've been able to see the lonely, sympathetic side. I've never really bought him as the evil Brimstone dealer, but this is proving to be worse anyhow--he truly is willing to sacrifice anyone (and I do mean anyone) to his grand scheme.<br /><br />Otherwise it was written well, with nice integration of the landscape--I think this is the first we've heard about deserted towns and the desolation of middle to west, but it makes sense in the America Harrison created. There's also a very neat twist on demon magic that merits applause. It's a new development for the world, and yet fully integrated with the magic system in place. That's a nice trick to pull off in book 9 of a series. <br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed it and finished it within a couple of days. To me it felt like a nice balance of action and down time--it's just not realistic or fun to be careening from one disaster to the next all the time. I enjoyed the world-building in the demon bar a great deal. It doesn't work very well as a stand-alone book at this point, but I'm sure most people wouldn't pick up book 9 without having read one or two other books in the series at least. Harrison does make an attempt to do a fast background/ context for readers, but it's very light on background. PNR fans might be disappointed as there is little emphasis on developing romantic intimacy. In all, it will definitely merit a re-read at some point, and might make it into my permanent collection.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3730531412776801524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122127052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122127052" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1497350-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1250569584p2/1497350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122127052?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/1497350-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1497350-kathryn?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1497350-kathryn?shelf=netgalley-or-first-reads">netgalley-or-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1497350-kathryn?shelf=demons">demons</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122127052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16469590601987027592">Pale Demon is book 9 in The Hollows series by Kim Harrison and all I can say is, if you have come this far, why stop now. Harrison has said that the series will roughly end with books 12-13, so though this book wrapped up some major storylines, I think a wonderful setup has happened and this is going to upset many readers. Not that I want to discourage anyone form reading this, but Rachel hooking up with a particular character has probably been at the top of many devoted reader lists. But not at</span>
  <span id="freeText16469590601987027592" style="display:none">Pale Demon is book 9 in The Hollows series by Kim Harrison and all I can say is, if you have come this far, why stop now. Harrison has said that the series will roughly end with books 12-13, so though this book wrapped up some major storylines, I think a wonderful setup has happened and this is going to upset many readers. Not that I want to discourage anyone form reading this, but Rachel hooking up with a particular character has probably been at the top of many devoted reader lists. But not at the top of mine. All I can say is, remember Kisten. Harrison is sneaky like that. I have been hoping for the story to go in the opposite direction of the setup here included and thankfully my hopes have not been dashed completely with this book. I think Harrison is setting up something interesting. <br /><br />The scene in Dalliance was brilliant. Harrison is extremely skilled at introducing numerous story lines and managing to keep everything coherent and eventualy tied together. This series is urban fantasy escapism at its best. I did not want the book to end and I can not recommend it enough. <br /><br />I find it difficult to discuss this book without mentioning spoilers so from here on out, I'm throwing caution to the wind and not worrying about spoilers....I have too much to talk about...<br /><br />Here there be SPOILERS<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />I realize that most people finishing this book are pinning their hopes on a relationship between Trent and Rachel. I do not want that and never have. I love rooting for the bad guy, the underdog, and Al is my forerunning contender, because no one has been as bad as Al, not Trent and not even Nick. I love Al and when you consider what Rachel learns about him in this book, how he has changed from the first book, and how he acts in this one, then I think there might be a real chance. Every thing is opposite here compared to the beginning of the series, with Trent and Al as the good guys, not the guys trying to kill Rachel. Harrison including that bit towards the end of the only demons who survived were the ones who could love is important and was said for a reason. I also thought it fitting that Trent was hurt by Al at the end. He killed tons of people letting the big bad demon loose and he could care less. Normaly this would bother Rachel but now she's willing to dismiss it because she is on the recieving end of Trent's interest? And Rachel is ok with Pierce remaining in the ever-after to be tortured by Al? This behavior does not fit with Rachel. I had expected her to rip the bracelet off and save him.<br /><br />I hope Rachel realizes that hiding behind Trent's bracelet is wrong, simply a choice to not accept herself. I loved it when Rachel finally admitted she was a demon and I felt she took a huge step backwards when choosing to keep the bracelet on. <br /><br />I did like the scene between Ivy and Rachel. I was happy that Ivy chose to move on. I expect an incredibly tragic scene in a later book, with Rachel able to save Ivy's soul. Save Ivy's soul and end up with Al. Then the series can end and not a monent earlier. <br /><br />And will someone please tell me the signifigance of the blue butterflies? </span>

<div id="review_147260553" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147260553" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147260553?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=hollows">hollows</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147260553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18282924139890588386">I might as well just say it. I loved this book. Loved. Loved. Loved this book. I read somewhere that this has been Kim Harrison's favorite book in the Hollows series so far and I can see why. I left feeling exhilarated --like absolutely anything could happen next. That is no small feat for the 9th book in a series; it would be so easy to let things to get stale.<br/><br/>Where do I begin? Well, begrudgingly, I can say I wasn't in love with the beginning of the book. As advertised, Rachel is taking a road </span>
  <span id="freeText18282924139890588386" style="display:none">I might as well just say it. I loved this book. Loved. Loved. Loved this book. I read somewhere that this has been Kim Harrison's favorite book in the Hollows series so far and I can see why. I left feeling exhilarated --like absolutely anything could happen next. That is no small feat for the 9th book in a series; it would be so easy to let things to get stale.<br /><br />Where do I begin? Well, begrudgingly, I can say I wasn't in love with the beginning of the book. As advertised, Rachel is taking a road trip from Cincinnati to San Francisco. She is going to the annual witches council meeting to get her shunning removed. Instead of her planned flight with Jenks... She ends up driving, in a car that's getting increasingly crowded... with an elf, a pixy, a vampire and two other witches. Rachel is struggling to stay alive as the council tries to get her before she reaches her destination. To complicate matters more, she is babysitting Trent, who is on a mysterious elf quest. And along the way, we meet a genetically engineered day-walking demon, who likes to eat souls and wreak havoc. Nothing Rachel can't handle, right?<br /><br />For me, the story hit its stride once Rachel faced off with the coven in San Francisco. And frankly, that was sooner than I expected. (I thought the road trip would last the whole book, but it was really more like 1/3 of it.) Her time in the ever-after is captivating. I loved having a peek inside the demon culture. I was enthralled getting to really know Al and Newt. And holy-freaking-cow, there was one scene at Al's place that blew me away. I think I read it four times before I could move on. I won't spoil it, but if you've read the book, you know the part I'm talking about.<br /><br />We have huge, huge developments surrounding what Rachel is and how she sees herself. We have (yet another) major shift in the relationship between Ivy and Rachel... one that leaves me wondering about their future. We see possibilities and (what appears to be) resolution surrounding Rachel's relationship with Pierce. And there are colossal changes in Rachel's feelings for Al and Trent.<br /><br />So much happens over the course of this book, when I look back to the beginning it's hard to believe it was all part of the same story. And even though we've "known" some of these characters since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30264.Dead_Witch_Walking__Rachel_Morgan_The_Hollows___1_" title="Dead Witch Walking (Rachel Morgan/The Hollows, #1) by Kim Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Dead Witch Walking</a>, I feel like we're really getting to see inside a few of them for the first time. And I love it. And I absolutely can not wait to see what happens next. I'd give it more than 5 stars if I could.<br /><br /><br />*ARC provided by NetGalley</span>
  <a data-text-id="18282924139890588386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16974095181912549435"><b>5++++++++ Stars to the Ever After and Beyond!</b><br/>Im not going to write a regular review for this book because there are already so many fantastic ones to read. But I will say, this is my third time reading this book and it gets me every time! I completely and absolutely LOVE this series but this book is the best of the bunch in my opinion. <i>Kim Harrison</i> writes her heart out in <i>The Hollows Series</i> but <u>Pale Demon</u> captured her soul and she was gracious enough to share it with the world! If you haven't re</span>
  <span id="freeText16974095181912549435" style="display:none"><b>5++++++++ Stars to the Ever After and Beyond!</b><br />Im not going to write a regular review for this book because there are already so many fantastic ones to read. But I will say, this is my third time reading this book and it gets me every time! I completely and absolutely LOVE this series but this book is the best of the bunch in my opinion. <i>Kim Harrison</i> writes her heart out in <i>The Hollows Series</i> but <u>Pale Demon</u> captured her soul and she was gracious enough to share it with the world! If you haven't read this series, you are seriously missing out on a world you will want to instantly become a part of and characters you will definitely never forget!</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4twSxPPjcVYS8qxTh0DIIvQzTgwR3HJ7vxidbf2xtqmqOTaFTpPNiptExhsYy145Xx2EVOalzYhY8ZSuP5xF6A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ErduCgjsv4sz4mr8zPXHrcwdgigPhEscmSZCIhU8gb1aUkpLtZwDV7pUALRTflG2ZzNIcPj99O9+z0vh1xFy/A==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText11622554846871390985" style="display:none">Kim Harrison is best known as the author of the New York Times #1 best selling Hollows series, but she has written more than urban fantasy and has published over two-dozen books spanning the gamut from young adult, thriller, several anthologies, and has scripted two original graphic novels.
